submarines to accommodate women</h1>\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"fusion-meta-info\"><div class=\"fusion-meta-info-wrapper\">By <span class=\"vcard\"><span class=\"fn\"><a class=\"fusion-clearfix\"></div></div></div>\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<br>\n\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"fusion-flexslider flexslider fusion-flexslider-loading post-slideshow fusion-post-slideshow\" style=\"height: 579px;\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<ul class=\"slides\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<li class=\"wp-caption flex-active-slide\" style=\"width: 100%; float: left; margin-right: -100%; position: relative; opacity: 1; display: block; z-index: 2;\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<img src=\"https://popularmilitary.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Submarines.jpg\" alt=\"\" draggable=\"false\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<p class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tSAN DIEGO (March 14, 2017) - Vice Adm. Nora W. Tyson, Commander, U.S. Third Fleet, addresses members and guests at the monthly Naval Submarine League (NSL) Luncheon on Naval Base Point Loma. The NSL is a professional organization for submariners and submarine advocates whose primary mission is to promote the general awareness of the importance of submarines to national security. (U.S. Navy photo by Mass Communication Specialist 1st Class Derek Stroop/Released)\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</p>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</li>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</ul>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<ol class=\"flex-control-nav flex-control-paging\"></ol><ul class=\"flex-direction-nav\"><li><a class=\"flex-prev flex-disabled\" href=\"#\" tabindex=\"-1\"></a></li><li><a class=\"flex-next flex-disabled\" href=\"#\" tabindex=\"-1\"></a></li></ul></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t<br>\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t<div class=\"post-content\">\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"content\">\n<p>PROVIDENCE, R.I. &nbsp;— Every <label class=\"highlight\">submarine</label> in the U.S. fleet was designed with the height, reach and strength of men in mind, from the way valves are placed to how display screens are angled.</p>\n<p>That’s going to change.</p>\n<p>With women now serving aboard <label class=\"highlight\">submarines</label>, defense contractor Electric Boat is designing what will be the first Navy subs built specifically to accommodate female crew members.</p>\n<p>The designers are doing the obvious things, such as adding more doors and washrooms to create separate sleeping and bathing areas for men and women and to give them more privacy. But they are also making more subtle modifications that may not have been in everyone’s periscope when the Navy admitted women into the Silent Service.</p>\n<p>For example, they are lowering some overhead valves and making them easier to turn, and installing steps in front of the triple-high bunk beds and stacked laundry machines.</p>\n<p>The first vessel built with some of the new features, the future USS New Jersey, is expected to be delivered to the Navy in 2021.</p>\n<p>The Navy lifted its ban on women on <label class=\"highlight\">submarines</label> in 2010, starting with officers. About 80 female officers and roughly 50 enlisted women are now serving on subs, and their numbers are expected to climb into the hundreds over the next few years.</p>\n<p>For now, the Navy is retrofitting existing subs with extra doors and designated washrooms to accommodate women. But Electric Boat in Groton, Connecticut, is at work on a redesign of the Navy’s Virginia-class fast-attack subs and is also developing a brand-new class of ballistic-missile <label class=\"highlight\">submarines</label>, relying on body measurements for both men and women.</p>\n<p>“We have a clean sheet of paper, so from the ground up, we’ll optimize for both men and women,” said Brian Wilson, Electric Boat director of the new ballistic-missile sub program.</p>\n<p>Electric Boat officials had no immediate estimate of how much the modifications will cost.</p>\n<!-- Quick Adsense WordPress Plugin: http://quicksense.net/ -->\n<div style=\"float:none;margin:10px -10px 10px -10px;text-align:center;\">\n<!-- /25580126/PopMil_300x250M_D -->\n<div id=\"div-gpt-ad-1446581284081-0\" style=\"height:250px; width:300px; margin:0 auto;\" data-google-query-id=\"CKCWlrHpudMCFRe5TwodmYINNg\">\n<script type=\"text/javascript\">\ngoogletag.cmd.push(function() { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1446581284081-0'); });\n</script>\n<div id=\"google_ads_iframe_/25580126/PopMil_300x250M_D_0__container__\" style=\"border: 0pt none;\"><iframe id=\"google_ads_iframe_/25580126/PopMil_300x250M_D_0\" title=\"3rd party ad content\" name=\"google_ads_iframe_/25580126/PopMil_300x250M_D_0\" width=\"300\" height=\"250\" scrolling=\"no\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;\"></iframe></div></div>\n</div>\n\n<p>As anyone who watches war movies knows, <label class=\"highlight\">submariners</label> are always turning valves, whether to operate machinery, redistribute water between tanks or isolate part of a system that has been damaged.</p>\n<p>On the <label class=\"highlight\">Columbia-class</label> boats, valves will generally be placed lower, Wilson said. Sometimes there will be an extension handle, and some will be easier to turn. Sailors will be able to connect their masks into the emergency air system at the side of passageways, instead of overhead.</p>\n<p>Emergency air masks are being moved on fast-attack <label class=\"highlight\">submarines</label>, too, but the bulk of the changes on those subs are to ensure privacy.</p>\n<p>Seats in the control room on the ballistic-missile <label class=\"highlight\">submarines</label> will adjust forward a little more so everyone can touch each display and reach every joystick. Steps will be added so shorter people can climb into the top bunk or see into the washers and dryers, since clothes that get stuck in the machines are a fire hazard.</p>\n<p>The first <label class=\"highlight\">Columbia-class</label> ballistic-missile sub is scheduled to join the fleet in 2031.</p>\n<p>At 5-foot-6, Lt. Marquette <label class=\"highlight\">Leveque</label>, one of the first women to serve on a <label class=\"highlight\">submarine</label>, said that she didn’t have any trouble reaching valves and other equipment but that the ergonomic changes will be helpful for shorter crewmates.</p>\n<p><label class=\"highlight\">Leveque</label> was assigned to a compartment with two other female officers on the USS Wyoming. They shared a washroom with male officers. A sign on the door could be flipped to show whether a man or woman was using it.</p>\n<p>With so few women on board, the timesharing worked, she said. But with more on the way, the need for separate spaces is greater, she added.</p>\n<p>“Privacy is important anywhere you are,” she said. “We live on this boat, as well as work there.”</p>\n<p>By JENNIFER McDERMOTT</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"copyright\">Copyright 2017 The Associated Press.
